<time>1622175721234</time><rate>5<//rate>< text>
They took a great one and made it even better! After a year's wait, when they changed locations, Mom's Tofu house is finally open again in South City.  Our patience was worth it - this location serves some of the best Korean food in the  area.
Highlights:
Home made tofu has an amazing silky texture, whether it's in an appetizer or one of the hot tofu soups. You can choose the spice level to taste - whatever you pick, the deep underlying flavor of the soup and protein comes through in spades.
Individually made rice portions. I didn't think I'd care, but this is a really nice touch. Fresh short grain Korean, wonderfully textured, accompanies your meal. This level of detail is apparent in all their dishes!
Barbeque - again, you can't go wrong, from the short ribs to the spicy chicken. Excellently done.
Each time we've come in (and we're regulars), the service is attentive,  personable and warm. I think the expansion in space (compared to the old location) has made for a better customer experience - there's space in between tables and enough staff to take care of each section well.
I love this place - it has a high spot in the regular rotation.< /text>

< Text>
Mom‚Äôs tofu is hands down my favorite restaurant in South San Francisco. I used to frequent the old location before they relocated. When I heard they were opening a new location, I was very excited. Excellent food and fantastic, friendly service. The secret behind their silken soft tofu is it that the tofu is made fresh on site. Furthermore, the rice is made to order. That‚Äôs right, the rice is prepared fresh for you. Portion sizes are filling and the side dishes are refreshing. Mom‚Äôs tofu is located downstairs inside the building. Give them a try!<//Text>

< text>
A really authentic Korean restaurant in California may not be so rare, but they are also not so accommodating to their dinner guests. We had my son's pet dog with us and so he searched online for a restaurant that would accept pets (dogs/cats) as dinner guests. We were delighted that they had a couple of table outside the front the restaurant., which perfected suited our ride-along pet. We were  visiting San Francisco since I was departing the next day, but we glad to have found a very tasty Korean meal at  pet-friendly restaurant. Good meal, great vibes. Most of the clientele were actually Korean-Americans, so you know it has to be authentic.</text>

< Review>
Small but popular Korean restaurant with a few vegetarian options, including a vegetarian bibimbap and broiled tofu with spicy vegetables. Fast, courteous service, and dinner entrees are served with a variety of pickled vegetables. A small cup of sweet Korean toasted rice punch ends each meal on a light note. Although the address is on Grand Avenue, the entrance is actually a few steps off Grand facing a small parking lot, so don't walk past by accident.</Review>

I am a regular there for a reason. Love the self serve side dishes and the food is delicious. The stone pot is always super hot, which is a requirement for good Korean bowl or soup.  It is definitely a home cook type of place.
If you get a chance, try the spicy chicken wings. Their special recipe makes it crispy and spicy.

4/19/19 Update: Mama's tofu no longer exist at the Grand Ave. in SSF.  There are few other locations on El Camino.<//text>

<user_id>110448983428808361581</user_id>< name>
Alice Jou</name>
<Time>1370833015789< /Time>< rate>
3<//rate>
< text>
I was expecting a little more. I liked the ban chan which came with kimchi, bean sprouts, radish, fish cake, potato salad, and a pancake. The chicken wings were cooked well, but the seasoning on the dry ones and the sauce on the wet ones weren't exciting. I enjoyed the short ribs, which were a good portion size and nice and tender but the tofu stew was a little bland and a bit skimpy on the meat.

I wouldn't mind giving it one more shot, but I wouldn't go out of my way to eat here.<//text>

<text>How I miss having a go-to Korean place around the corner. This isn't exactly around the corner from me, but I think it's my new guilty pleasure!

The restaurant is small but has plenty of tables. Turnaround is really fast so you don't have to wait too long to get a seat. It was packed on a Thursday night at 8pm.

Lots of banchan and you get a small sized veggie pancake for free too. Service is awesome. We got 2 tofu soups and 1 kalbi. The kalbi was great and came first. It was a heaping pile! The tofu soup left something to be desired. I like that they give you an egg (some places don't give you one!). But I asked for medium spicy and it wasn't spicy at all. The broth was very thin and not that flavorful. Maybe that's just how they make it versus other places? I don't know.

(Free parking is awesome.)<//text><pictures>None<//pictures>< resp>

< Rate>
4</Rate>
<text>Mom's Tofu House is a small little Korean restaurant tucked away on Grand Ave...with some great Korean dishes!

I usually come here during my lunch break from work, and as long as you get there before noon, you'll be able to get a seat and a table without a wait. Once the clock strikes noon however, the people from the surrounding areas start trickling in, and before you know it, you're hit with a mass of people on their lunch break, all waiting for a seat and table. If you get there after noon, you might have to wait a bit before getting a table.

The best part about this place is that the mini Korean side dishes (kimchi, fish cake, salad, potatoes, etc.) are all placed together in a side bar area. This side bar area is self serve and you can refill your own plate as many times as you want.

Along with the unlimited side dishes, I usually also order a spicy beef soon dubu (beef tofu soup) which comes with an egg (crack it open and throw it in your soup) and a small bowl of steamed white rice. There are 5 levels of spiciness, and I find the 4th level (spicy) to be the most optimal. Anything more than the 4th level is too spicy to be enjoyable.

Prices are relatively cheap (as far as Korean places go), and the service is quick and friendly.

I would definitely recommend this place for lunch!</text><Pics>None<//Pics><resp>None<//resp>< Gmap_id>
0x808f796c438637d3:0xbd71258409ed4dc5</Gmap_id>

< text>
Low key lunch or dinner spot in SSF. Definitely come here for either the soft tofu soups (their specialty) or the lunch bento specials. As with other Korean places, the banchan side dishes are complementary. There are about 6-8 different banchans, and sometimes they throw in a complementary kimchi pancake. For lunch, the banchan is buffet style, so you can grab as much as you want (but don't be wasteful!).Their lunch special bentos are a good size, with a protein + rice, japchae noodles, a dumpling, buffet style banchan, and a small miso soup. Definitely a great place for lunch, though it's small, so it's best to go with a group of 6 people or less.< /text>

<review>I bought a lower end vehicle from them back in May 2020, a 2015 Toyota Corolla with 53k miles

I have myself to blame as I didn't bother inspecting the vehicle myself, based off the high end cars, I just trusted off the look that all would be good.

Well after the fact and signing off paperwork, I looked at my purchased vehicle, all 4 tires were cracking, I was able to drive 5 months, 3-3,500 miles before the wobbling/braking finally got so bad and I bought new tires in October 2020 for $520

The right rear window wouldn't go down from the time I bought the car from the master switch or the right rear itself, one of cheaper fixes I've had on this card.

About a week after delivery, the AC stopped blowing cold, it was evident the car was just filled with Freeon to avoid them replacing the AC condenser. My mechanic took care of this and when he took apart the parts, the current condenser parts were from a different year, which tells me the car definitely had a front impact damage at some point

There is visible gap on the front bumper, along with the paint starting to peel off about a month in, (flat black paint btw) not pearl like the actual paint.

I fixed the serpentine belt at 57k miles, no biggie, what was big and unexpected was yesterday's repair of a motor mount, 2 wheel bearings, and sway bar links, which to be honest, there was a clunk noise from the get go, but my mechanic didn't notice an issue in the beginning

It's obvious this car was just took on trade, prettied up, pics taken and put up for sale, I'm expecting a response showing we inspect all cars, if so, ask for an inspection report, if one is not presented right there and then, then you know they're buying time to make one up, and in my case I wouldn't have had to go smog the car myself because they "forgot "

Again 95% of it falls on me for not looking at the car, I do thank Kifah for helping me get my loan, and the interest rate he helped me get, he's a great guy, sadly this falls on the car dealerships ownership, not him.

Sure I did get a small discount, but getting an unsafe car(cracked tires, no smog etc) doesn't validate that.

Please make sure to get your possible purchase inspected by a mechanic of YOUR choosing, ask for a multi point inspection report done by them before posting(they must have one in each cars deal jacket) and remember Carfax isn't everything, a car can have a previous accident and go unreported if fixed under the table, like in the case of my vehicle.<//review><Pics>None<//Pics>< response>

< text>
Asian friends took me here.
Bland Laos food. The Pho is not good. They skimp on so many ingredients that would make it authentic. The pho has minced cilantro, 1 strip of paper thin beef flank and 2 meatballs and broth. Thats it.....Really?
The food is stripped of its bountiful Real flavors..maybe to reduce cost....which is disappointing. The female behind the register in her late 30's is snobby and impatient. The pizza here is some of the best I've had in the San Fernando Valley. The ingredients are excellent. My usual go to is the Truffle pizza - simple, yet delicious. I liked the way the ordering process was before, where you would order as you go down the line where all the ingredients are. Because this is simply not the process anymore, that's why I deducted a star. The service also used to be slightly better, and not sure exactly why but my pizzas the last couple times have been burnt. I'm not sure if it was just left too long in the oven or what the issue was, but the flavors were there. Despite these small issues, I highly recommend this place !</review>
